legend</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background-color:#ebebeb;"><a href="/wiki/Parapsychology" title="Parapsychology">Parapsychology</a></div><div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Death_and_culture" title="Death and culture">Death and culture</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parapsychology" title="Parapsychology">Parapsychology</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scientific_literacy" title="Scientific literacy">Scientific literacy</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Paranormal" title="Template:Paranormal"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Paranormal" title="Template talk:Paranormal"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Paranormal&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Astrology</b> is the study of the movements and relative positions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestial_objects" title="Celestial objects">celestial objects</a> as a means of <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divining</a> information about human affairs and terrestrial events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Astrology has been dated to at least the 2nd millennium BCE, and has its roots in <a href="/wiki/Calendrical_calculation" title="Calendrical calculation">calendrical</a> systems used to predict seasonal shifts and to interpret celestial cycles as signs of divine communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword,_11_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword,_11-4">[4]</a></sup> Many cultures have attached importance to astronomical events, and some&#8212;such as the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a>&#8212;developed elaborate systems for predicting terrestrial events from celestial observations. <a href="/wiki/Western_astrology" title="Western astrology">Western astrology</a>, one of the oldest astrological systems still in use, can trace its roots to 19th&#8211;17th century <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">BCE</a> <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, from which it spread to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a> and eventually <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. Contemporary Western astrology is often associated with systems of <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscopes</a> that purport to explain aspects of a person\'s <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a> and predict significant events in their lives based on the positions of celestial objects; the majority of professional astrologers rely on such systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cosmic_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmic-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>83</span></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout most of its history, astrology was considered a scholarly tradition and was common in academic circles, often in close relation with <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alchemy" title="Alchemy">alchemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorology</a>, and medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kassell_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kassell-6">[6]</a></sup> It was present in political circles and is mentioned in various works of literature, from <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a> to <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lope_de_Vega" title="Lope de Vega">Lope de Vega</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Calder%C3%B3n_de_la_Barca" title="Pedro Calder&#243;n de la Barca">Calder&#243;n de la Barca</a>.\nFollowing the end of the 19th century and the wide-scale adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific method</a>, astrology has been challenged successfully on both <a href="/wiki/Scientific_theory" title="Scientific theory">theoretical</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vishveshwara_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vishveshwara-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>249;</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AsquithNSF_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-AsquithNSF-8">[8]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Experiment" title="Experiment">experimental</a> grounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carlson_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carlson-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zarka_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zarka-10">[10]</a></sup> and has been shown to have no scientific validity or <a href="/wiki/Explanatory_power" title="Explanatory power">explanatory power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cosmic_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmic-5">[5]</a></sup> Astrology thus lost its academic and theoretical standing, and common belief in it has largely declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brit_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-11">[11]</a></sup> While polls have demonstrated that approximately one quarter of American, British, and Canadian people say they continue to believe that star and planet positions affect their lives,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> astrology is now recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>&#8212;a belief that is incorrectly presented as scientific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thagard_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thagard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SandPSandAstroSoc_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-SandPSandAstroSoc-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astrosociety.org_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-astrosociety.org-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hartmann_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hartmann-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="403" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg/170px-Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg/255px-Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg/340px-Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marcantonio_Raimondi" title="Marcantonio Raimondi">Marcantonio Raimondi</a> engraving, 15th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The word <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/astrology" title="wikt:astrology">astrology</a></i> comes from the early <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/astrologia" title="wikt:astrologia">astrologia</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> which derives from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%80%CF%83%CF%84%CF%81%CE%BF%CE%BB%CE%BF%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1" title="wikt:&#7936;&#963;&#964;&#961;&#959;&#955;&#959;&#947;&#943;&#945;">&#7936;&#963;&#964;&#961;&#959;&#955;&#959;&#947;&#943;&#945;</a></span>&#8212;from <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%84%CF%83%CF%84%CF%81%CE%BF%CE%BD#Ancient_Greek" title="wikt:&#7940;&#963;&#964;&#961;&#959;&#957;">&#7940;&#963;&#964;&#961;&#959;&#957;</a> <i>astron</i> ("star") and <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-%CE%BB%CE%BF%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1#Ancient_Greek" title="wikt:-&#955;&#959;&#947;&#943;&#945;">-&#955;&#959;&#947;&#943;&#945;</a> <i>-logia</i>, ("study of"&#8212;"account of the stars"). <i>Astrologia</i> later passed into meaning \'star-divination\' with <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/astronomia" title="wikt:astronomia">astronomia</a></i> used for the scientific term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_astrology" title="History of astrology">History of astrology</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1869" data-file-width="1325" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg/170px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg/255px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg/340px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Zodiac Man</i> a diagram of a human body and astrological symbols with instructions explaining the importance of astrology from a medical perspective. From a 15th-century Welsh manuscript</div></div></div>\n<p>Many cultures have attached importance to astronomical events, and the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> developed elaborate systems for predicting terrestrial events from celestial observations. In the West, astrology most often consists of a system of <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscopes</a> purporting to explain aspects of a person\'s <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a> and predict future events in their life based on the positions of the sun, moon, and other celestial objects at the time of their birth. The majority of professional astrologers rely on such systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cosmic_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmic-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>83</span></sup>\n</p><p>Astrology has been dated to at least the 2nd millennium <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BCE" title="BCE">BCE</a>, with roots in <a href="/wiki/Calendrical_calculation" title="Calendrical calculation">calendrical</a> systems used to predict seasonal shifts and to interpret celestial cycles as signs of divine communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword,_11_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword,_11-4">[4]</a></sup> A form of astrology was practised in the first dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (1950&#8211;1651 BCE). Chinese astrology was elaborated in the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> (1046&#8211;256 BCE). <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_astrology" title="Hellenistic astrology">Hellenistic astrology</a> after 332 BCE mixed <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astrology" title="Babylonian astrology">Babylonian astrology</a> with Egyptian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decans" title="Decans">Decanic astrology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, creating <a href="/wiki/Horoscopic_astrology" title="Horoscopic astrology">horoscopic astrology</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great\'s</a> conquest of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> allowed astrology to spread to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>. In Rome, astrology was associated with \'<a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">Chaldean</a> wisdom\'. After the conquest of Alexandria in the 7th century, astrology was taken up by Islamic scholars, and Hellenistic texts were translated into Arabic and Persian. In the 12th century, Arabic texts were imported to Europe and <a href="/wiki/Latin_translations_of_the_12th_century" title="Latin translations of the 12th century">translated into Latin</a>. Major astronomers including <a href="/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="Tycho Brahe">Tycho Brahe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galileo" title="Galileo">Galileo</a> practised as court astrologers. Astrological references appear in literature in the works of poets such as <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a>, and of playwrights such as <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Marlowe" title="Christopher Marlowe">Christopher Marlowe</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>.\n</p><p>Throughout most of its history, astrology was considered a scholarly tradition. It was accepted in political and academic contexts, and was connected with other studies, such as <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alchemy" title="Alchemy">alchemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorology</a>, and medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kassell_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kassell-6">[6]</a></sup> At the end of the 17th century, new scientific concepts in astronomy and physics (such as <a href="/wiki/Heliocentrism" title="Heliocentrism">heliocentrism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">Newtonian mechanics</a>) called astrology into question. Astrology thus lost its academic and theoretical standing, and common belief in astrology has largely declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brit_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_world">Ancient world</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astrology" title="Babylonian astrology">Babylonian astrology</a></div>\n<p>Astrology, in its broadest sense, is the search for meaning in the sky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2,3</span></sup> Early evidence for humans making conscious attempts to measure, record, and predict seasonal changes by reference to astronomical cycles, appears as markings on bones and cave walls, which show that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_cycle" title="Lunar cycle">lunar cycles</a> were being noted as early as 25,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshack_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshack-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>81ff</span></sup> This was a first step towards recording the Moon\'s influence upon tides and rivers, and towards organising a communal calendar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshack_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marshack-21">[21]</a></sup> Farmers addressed agricultural needs with increasing knowledge of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constellations" title="Constellations">constellations</a> that appear in the different seasons&#8212;and used the rising of particular star-groups to herald annual floods or seasonal activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> By the 3rd millennium BCE, civilisations had sophisticated awareness of celestial cycles, and may have oriented temples in alignment with <a href="/wiki/Heliacal_rising" title="Heliacal rising">heliacal risings</a> of the stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scattered evidence suggests that the oldest known astrological references are copies of texts made in the ancient world. The <a href="/wiki/Venus_tablet_of_Ammisaduqa" title="Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa">Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa</a> is thought to be compiled in <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a> around 1700 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>  A scroll documenting an early use of <a href="/wiki/Electional_astrology" title="Electional astrology">electional astrology</a> is doubtfully ascribed to the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumerian</a> ruler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gudea_of_Lagash" title="Gudea of Lagash">Gudea of Lagash</a> (c. 2144 &#8211; 2124 BCE). This describes how the gods revealed to him in a dream the constellations that would be most favourable for the planned construction of a temple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> However, there is controversy about whether these were genuinely recorded at the time or merely ascribed to ancient rulers by posterity. The oldest undisputed evidence of the use of astrology as an integrated system of knowledge is therefore attributed to the records of the first dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (1950&#8211;1651 BCE). This astrology had some parallels with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> Greek (western) astrology, including the zodiac, a norming point near 9 degrees in Aries, the trine aspect, planetary exaltations, and the dodekatemoria (the twelve divisions of 30 degrees each).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rochberg-Halton_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rochberg-Halton-26">[26]</a></sup> The Babylonians viewed celestial events as possible signs rather than as causes of physical events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rochberg-Halton_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rochberg-Halton-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The system of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese astrology</a> was elaborated during the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> (1046&#8211;256 BCE) and flourished during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" title="Han Dynasty">Han Dynasty</a> (2nd century BCE to 2nd century CE), during which all the familiar elements of traditional Chinese culture &#8211; the Yin-Yang philosophy, theory of the five elements, Heaven and Earth, Confucian morality &#8211; were brought together to formalise the philosophical principles of Chinese medicine and divination, astrology and alchemy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kistemaker_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kistemaker-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3,4</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_objections">Ancient objections</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1636" data-file-width="1227" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG/170px-Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG/255px-Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG/340px-Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Roman orator <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a> objected to astrology</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a> stated the twins objection (that with close birth times, personal outcomes can be very different), later developed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Augustine" title="Saint Augustine">Saint Augustine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> He argued that since the other planets are much more distant from the earth than the moon, they could have only very tiny influence compared to the moon\'s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> He also argued that if astrology explains everything about a person\'s fate, then it wrongly ignores the visible effect of inherited ability and parenting, changes in health worked by medicine, or the effects of the weather on people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Plotinus" title="Plotinus">Plotinus</a> argued that since the fixed stars are much more distant than the planets, it is laughable to imagine the planets\' effect on human affairs should depend on their position with respect to the zodiac. He also argues that the interpretation of the moon\'s <a href="/wiki/Conjunction_(astronomy)" title="Conjunction (astronomy)">conjunction</a> with a planet as good when the moon is full, but bad when the moon is waning, is clearly wrong, as from the moon\'s point of view, half of its surface is always in sunlight; and from the planet\'s point of view, waning should be better, as then the planet sees some light from the moon, but when the moon is full to us, it is dark, and therefore bad, on the side facing the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Favorinus" title="Favorinus">Favorinus</a> argued that it was absurd to imagine that stars and planets would affect human bodies in the same way as they affect the tides,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and equally absurd that small motions in the heavens cause large changes in people\'s fates. <a href="/wiki/Sextus_Empiricus" title="Sextus Empiricus">Sextus Empiricus</a> argued that it was absurd to link human attributes with myths about the signs of the zodiac.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carneades" title="Carneades">Carneades</a> argued that belief in fate denies <a href="/wiki/Free_will" title="Free will">free will</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">morality</a>; that people born at different times can all die in the same accident or battle; and that contrary to uniform influences from the stars, tribes and cultures are all different.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hellenistic_Egypt">Hellenistic Egypt</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_astrology" title="Hellenistic astrology">Hellenistic astrology</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quadritpartitum.jpg"><img alt="Ptolemy\'s Tetrabiblos, the Hellenistic text that founded Western astrology" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="419" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Quadritpartitum.jpg/170px-Quadritpartitum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Quadritpartitum.jpg/255px-Quadritpartitum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Quadritpartitum.jpg/340px-Quadritpartitum.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quadritpartitum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1484 copy of first page of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy\'s</a> <i>Tetrabiblos</i>, translated into Latin by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plato_of_Tivoli" title="Plato of Tivoli">Plato of Tivoli</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 525 BCE, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> was conquered by the Persians. The 1st century BCE Egyptian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dendera_Zodiac" title="Dendera Zodiac">Dendera Zodiac</a> shares two signs &#8211; the Balance and the Scorpion &#8211; with Mesopotamian astrology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the occupation by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> in 332 BCE, Egypt became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a>. The city of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> was founded by Alexander after the conquest, becoming the place where <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astrology" title="Babylonian astrology">Babylonian astrology</a> was mixed with Egyptian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decans" title="Decans">Decanic astrology</a> to create <a href="/wiki/Horoscopic_astrology" title="Horoscopic astrology">Horoscopic astrology</a>. This contained the Babylonian zodiac with its system of planetary <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_(astrology)" title="Exaltation (astrology)">exaltations</a>, the triplicities of the signs and the importance of eclipses. It used the Egyptian concept of dividing the zodiac into thirty-six decans of ten degrees each, with an emphasis on the rising decan, and the Greek system of planetary Gods, sign rulership and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four_elements" title="Four elements">four elements</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> 2nd century BCE texts predict positions of planets in zodiac signs at the time of the rising of certain decans, particularly Sothis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astrologer" title="Astrologer">astrologer</a> and astronomer <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy#Astrology" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> lived in Alexandria. Ptolemy\'s work the <i><a href="/wiki/Tetrabiblos" title="Tetrabiblos">Tetrabiblos</a></i> formed the basis of Western astrology, and, "...enjoyed almost the authority of a Bible among the astrological writers of a thousand years or more."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece_and_Rome">Greece and Rome</span></h3>\n<p>The conquest of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> exposed the Greeks to ideas from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, Babylon, Persia and central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Around 280 BCE, <a href="/wiki/Berossus" title="Berossus">Berossus</a>, a priest of <a href="/wiki/Marduk" title="Marduk">Bel</a> from Babylon, moved to the Greek island of <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">Kos</a>, teaching astrology and Babylonian culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> By the 1st century BCE, there were two varieties of astrology, one using <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscopes</a> to describe the past, present and future; the other, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theurgic" title="Theurgic">theurgic</a>, emphasising the <a href="/wiki/Soul" title="Soul">soul\'s</a> ascent to the stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Greek influence played a crucial role in the transmission of astrological theory to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B32_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-B32-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first definite reference to astrology in Rome comes from the orator <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Elder" title="Cato the Elder">Cato</a>, who in 160 BCE warned farm overseers against consulting with Chaldeans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> who were described as Babylonian \'star-gazers\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion227_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campion227-44">[44]</a></sup> Among both Greeks and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, Babylonia (also known as <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">Chaldea</a>) became so identified with astrology that \'Chaldean wisdom\' became <a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">synonymous</a> with <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> using planets and stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>  The 2nd-century Roman poet and satirist <a href="/wiki/Juvenal" title="Juvenal">Juvenal</a> complains about the pervasive influence of Chaldeans, saying, "Still more trusted are the Chaldaeans; every word uttered by the astrologer they will believe has come from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_(mythology)" title="Jupiter (mythology)">Hammon\'s</a> fountain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the first astrologers to bring <a href="/wiki/Hermeticism" title="Hermeticism">Hermetic</a> astrology to Rome was <a href="/wiki/Thrasyllus_of_Mendes" title="Thrasyllus of Mendes">Thrasyllus</a>, astrologer to the <a href="/wiki/Emperor" title="Emperor">emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B32_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-B32-42">[42]</a></sup> the first emperor to have had a court astrologer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> though his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> had used astrology to help legitimise his <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">Imperial</a> rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_world">Medieval world</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindu">Hindu</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Hindu astrology</a></div>\n<p>The main texts upon which classical Indian astrology is based are early medieval compilations, notably the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%E1%B9%9Bhat_Par%C4%81%C5%9Bara_Hor%C4%81%C5%9B%C4%81stra" title="B&#7771;hat Par&#257;&#347;ara Hor&#257;&#347;&#257;stra"><i lang="sa-Latn" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit transliteration">B&#7771;hat Par&#257;&#347;ara Hor&#257;&#347;&#257;stra</i></a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/S%C4%81r%C4%81val%C4%AB" title="S&#257;r&#257;val&#299;">S&#257;r&#257;val&#299;</a></i> by <i lang="sa-Latn" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit transliteration">Kaly&#257;&#7751;avarma</i>.\nThe <i>Hor&#257;shastra</i> is a composite work of 71 chapters, of which the first part  (chapters 1&#8211;51) dates to the 7th to early 8th centuries and the second part (chapters 52&#8211;71) to the later 8th century. The <i>S&#257;r&#257;val&#299;</i> likewise dates to around 800 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> English translations of these texts were published by N.N. Krishna Rau and V.B. Choudhari in 1963 and 1961, respectively.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic">Islamic</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Astrology_in_medieval_Islam" title="Astrology in medieval Islam">Astrology in medieval Islam</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg"><img alt="Image of a Latin astrological text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1622" data-file-width="2419" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg/220px-Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg/330px-Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg/440px-Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> translation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albumasar" title="Albumasar">Ab&#363; Ma&#703;shar\'s</a> <i>De Magnis Coniunctionibus</i> (\'Of the great <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conjunction_(astronomy_and_astrology)" title="Conjunction (astronomy and astrology)">conjunctions</a>\'), <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, 1515</div></div></div>\n<p>Astrology was taken up by Islamic scholars<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> following the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> to the Arabs in the 7th century, and the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid empire</a> in the 8th. The second Abbasid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">caliph</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Mansur" title="Al Mansur">Al Mansur</a> (754&#8211;775) founded the city of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> to act as a centre of learning, and included in its design a library-translation centre known as <i>Bayt al-Hikma</i> \'House of Wisdom\', which continued to receive development from his heirs and was to provide a major impetus for Arabic-Persian translations of Hellenistic astrological texts. The early translators included <a href="/wiki/Mashallah_ibn_Athari" title="Mashallah ibn Athari">Mashallah</a>, who helped to elect the time for the foundation of Baghdad,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biruni_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biruni-51">[51]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sahl_ibn_Bishr" title="Sahl ibn Bishr">Sahl ibn Bishr</a>, (<i>a.k.a.</i> <i>Zael</i>), whose texts were directly influential upon later European astrologers such as <a href="/wiki/Guido_Bonatti" title="Guido Bonatti">Guido Bonatti</a> in the 13th century, and <a href="/wiki/William_Lilly" title="William Lilly">William Lilly</a> in the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Knowledge of Arabic texts started to become imported into Europe during the <a href="/wiki/Latin_translations_of_the_12th_century" title="Latin translations of the 12th century">Latin translations of the 12th century</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1907" data-file-width="1409" decoding="async" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg/170px-Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg/255px-Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg/340px-Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> meets the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian</a> in the Sphere of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>, in Canto 5 of the <i><a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Dante)" title="Paradiso (Dante)">Paradiso</a></i></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_astrology" title="Christian views on astrology">Christian views on astrology</a></div>\n<p>The first astrological book published in Europe was the <i>Liber Planetis et Mundi Climatibus</i> ("Book of the Planets and Regions of the World"), which appeared between 1010 and 1027 AD, and may have been authored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerbert_of_Aurillac" title="Gerbert of Aurillac">Gerbert of Aurillac</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion44_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campion44-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy\'s</a> second century AD <i><a href="/wiki/Tetrabiblos" title="Tetrabiblos">Tetrabiblos</a></i> was translated into Latin by <a href="/wiki/Plato_Tiburtinus" title="Plato Tiburtinus">Plato of Tivoli</a> in 1138.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion44_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campion44-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_order" title="Dominican order">Dominican</a> theologian <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> followed <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> in proposing that the stars ruled the imperfect \'sublunary\' body, while attempting to reconcile astrology with Christianity by stating that God ruled the soul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion45_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campion45-54">[54]</a></sup> The thirteenth century mathematician <a href="/wiki/Campanus_of_Novara" title="Campanus of Novara">Campanus of Novara</a> is said to have devised a system of astrological houses that divides the <a href="/wiki/Prime_vertical" title="Prime vertical">prime vertical</a> into \'houses\' of equal 30&#176; arcs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion46_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campion46-55">[55]</a></sup> though the system was used earlier in the East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The thirteenth century <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">astronomer</a> <a href="/wiki/Guido_Bonatti" title="Guido Bonatti">Guido Bonatti</a> wrote a textbook, the <i>Liber Astronomicus</i>, a copy of which King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a> owned at the end of the fifteenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion46_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campion46-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Dante)" title="Paradiso (Dante)">Paradiso</a></i>, the final part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Divine_Comedy" title="Divine Comedy">Divine Comedy</a></i>, the Italian poet <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> referred "in countless details"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Durling_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Durling-57">[57]</a></sup> to the astrological planets, though he adapted traditional astrology to suit his Christian viewpoint,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Durling_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Durling-57">[57]</a></sup> for example using astrological thinking in his prophecies of the reform of Christendom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_objections">Medieval objections</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3009" data-file-width="2705" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg/170px-Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg/255px-Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg/340px-Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The medieval theologian <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a> criticised the predictive part of astrology</div></div></div>\n<p>In the seventh century, <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a> argued in his <i><a href="/wiki/Etymologiae" title="Etymologiae">Etymologiae</a></i> that astronomy described the movements of the heavens, while astrology had two parts: one was scientific, describing the movements of the sun, the moon and the stars, while the other, making predictions, was theologically erroneous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood5_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wood5-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Isidore_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Isidore-60">[60]</a></sup> In contrast, <a href="/wiki/John_Gower" title="John Gower">John Gower</a> in the fourteenth century defined astrology as essentially limited to the making of predictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood5_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wood5-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The influence of the stars was in turn divided into natural astrology, with for example effects on tides and the growth of plants, and judicial astrology, with supposedly predictable effects on people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood6_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wood6-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen148_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allen148-63">[63]</a></sup> The fourteenth century sceptic <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Oresme" title="Nicole Oresme">Nicole Oresme</a> however included astronomy as a part of astrology in his <i>Livre de divinacions</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood8_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wood8-64">[64]</a></sup> Oresme argued that current approaches to prediction of events such as plagues, wars, and weather were inappropriate, but that such prediction was a valid field of inquiry. However, he attacked the use of astrology to choose the timing of actions (so-called interrogation and election) as wholly false, and rejected the determination of human action by the stars on grounds of free will.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood8_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wood8-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coopland_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coopland-65">[65]</a></sup> The friar Laurens Pignon (c. 1368&#8211;1449)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> similarly rejected all forms of divination and determinism, including by the stars, in his 1411 <i>Contre les Devineurs</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> This was in opposition to the tradition carried by the Arab astronomer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albumasar" title="Albumasar">Albumasar</a> (787-886) whose <i>Introductorium in Astronomiam</i> and <i>De Magnis Coniunctionibus</i> argued the view that both individual actions and larger scale history are determined by the stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_and_Early_Modern">Renaissance and Early Modern</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="386" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg/220px-Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg/330px-Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\'An Astrologer Casting a Horoscope\' from <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fludd" title="Robert Fludd">Robert Fludd\'s</a> <i>Utriusque Cosmi Historia</i>, 1617</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> scholars commonly practised astrology. <a href="/wiki/Gerolamo_Cardano" title="Gerolamo Cardano">Gerolamo Cardano</a> cast the horoscope of king <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI_of_England" title="Edward VI of England">Edward VI of England</a>, while <a href="/wiki/John_Dee" title="John Dee">John Dee</a> was the personal astrologer to queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_de_Medici" title="Catherine de Medici">Catherine de Medici</a> paid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Nostradamus" title="Michael Nostradamus">Michael Nostradamus</a> in 1566 to verify the prediction of the death of her husband, king <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II of France</a> made by her astrologer Lucus Gauricus. Major astronomers who practised as court astrologers included <a href="/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="Tycho Brahe">Tycho Brahe</a> in the royal court of Denmark, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburgs" title="Habsburgs">Habsburgs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medici" title="Medici">Medici</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno" title="Giordano Bruno">Giordano Bruno</a> who was burnt at the stake for heresy in Rome in 1600.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion47_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campion47-69">[69]</a></sup> The distinction between astrology and astronomy was not entirely clear. Advances in astronomy were often motivated by the desire to improve the accuracy of astrology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ephemeris" title="Ephemeris">Ephemerides</a> with complex astrological calculations, and <a href="/wiki/Almanac" title="Almanac">almanacs</a> interpreting celestial events for use in medicine and for choosing times to plant crops, were popular in Elizabethan England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harkness105_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harkness105-71">[71]</a></sup> In 1597, the English <a href="/wiki/Mathematician" title="Mathematician">mathematician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hood_(mathematician)" title="Thomas Hood (mathematician)">Thomas Hood</a> made a set of paper instruments that used revolving overlays to help students work out relationships between fixed stars or constellations, the midheaven, and the twelve <a href="/wiki/House_(astrology)" title="House (astrology)">astrological houses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harkness133_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harkness133-72">[72]</a></sup> Hood\'s instruments also illustrated, for pedagogical purposes, the supposed relationships between the signs of the zodiac, the planets, and the parts of the human body adherents believed were governed by the planets and signs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harkness133_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Harkness133-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> While Hood\'s presentation was innovative, his astrological information was largely standard and was taken from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerard_Mercator" title="Gerard Mercator">Gerard Mercator\'s</a> astrological disc made in 1551, or a source used by Mercator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p><p>English astrology had reached its zenith by the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Astrologers were theorists, researchers, and social engineers, as well as providing individual advice to everyone from monarchs downwards. Among other things, astrologers could advise on the best time to take a journey or harvest a crop, diagnose and prescribe for physical or mental illnesses, and predict natural disasters. This underpinned a system in which everything&#8212;people, the world, the universe&#8212;was understood to be interconnected, and astrology co-existed happily with <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magic_(paranormal)" title="Magic (paranormal)">magic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlightenment_period_and_onwards">Enlightenment period and onwards</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="458" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg/220px-Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg/330px-Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg/440px-Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seven_spiritualists_1906.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle-class" title="Middle-class">Middle-class</a> Chicago women discuss spiritualism (1906)</div></div></div>\n<p>During <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Enlightenment" title="The Enlightenment">the Enlightenment</a>, intellectual sympathy for astrology fell away, leaving only a popular following supported by cheap almanacs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porter_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Porter-78">[78]</a></sup> One English almanac compiler, Richard Saunders, followed the spirit of the age by printing a derisive <i>Discourse on the Invalidity of Astrology</i>, while in France <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Bayle" title="Pierre Bayle">Pierre Bayle\'s</a> <i>Dictionnaire</i> of 1697 stated that the subject was puerile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porter_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Porter-78">[78]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Satire" title="Satire">satirist</a> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Swift" title="Jonathan Swift">Jonathan Swift</a> ridiculed the <a href="/wiki/Whiggism" title="Whiggism">Whig</a> political astrologer <a href="/wiki/John_Partridge_(astrologer)" title="John Partridge (astrologer)">John Partridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porter_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-Porter-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Astrology saw a popular revival starting in the 19th century, as part of a general revival of <a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">spiritualism</a> and&#8212;later, <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> philosophy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion-2009_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campion-2009-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>239&#8211;249</span></sup> and through the influence of mass media such as newspaper horoscopes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion-2009_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campion-2009-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>259&#8211;263</span></sup> Early in the 20th century the psychiatrist <a href="/wiki/Carl_Jung" title="Carl Jung">Carl Jung</a> developed some concepts concerning astrology,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> which led to the development of <a href="/wiki/Psychological_astrology" title="Psychological astrology">psychological astrology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campion-2009_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-Campion-2009-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>251&#8211;256;</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Principles_and_practice">Principles and practice</span></h2>\n<p>Advocates have defined astrology as a symbolic language, an <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> form, a <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, and a method of divination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Though most cultural astrology systems share common roots in ancient philosophies that influenced each other, many use methods that differ from those in the West. These include Hindu astrology (also known as "Indian astrology" and in modern times referred to as "Vedic astrology") and Chinese astrology, both of which have influenced the world\'s cultural history.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western">Western</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Western_astrology" title="Western astrology">Western astrology</a> is a form of <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> based on the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscope</a> for an exact moment, such as a person\'s birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> It uses the tropical zodiac, which is aligned to the <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">equinoctial points</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Western astrology is founded on the movements and relative positions of celestial bodies such as the Sun, Moon and planets, which are analysed by their movement through <a href="/wiki/Astrological_sign" title="Astrological sign">signs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Zodiac" title="Zodiac">zodiac</a> (twelve spatial divisions of the <a href="/wiki/Ecliptic" title="Ecliptic">ecliptic</a>) and by their <a href="/wiki/Astrological_aspect" title="Astrological aspect">aspects</a> (based on geometric angles) relative to one another. They are also considered by their placement in <a href="/wiki/House_(astrology)" title="House (astrology)">houses</a> (twelve spatial divisions of the sky).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Astrology\'s modern representation in western popular media is usually reduced to <a href="/wiki/Sun_sign_astrology" title="Sun sign astrology">sun sign astrology</a>, which considers only the zodiac sign of the Sun at an individual\'s date of birth, and represents only 1/12 of the total chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The horoscope visually expresses the set of relationships for the time and place of the chosen event. These relationships are between the seven \'planets\', signifying tendencies such as war and love; the twelve signs of the zodiac; and the twelve houses. Each planet is in a particular sign and a particular house at the chosen time, when observed from the chosen place, creating two kinds of relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kremer_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kremer-89">[89]</a></sup> A third kind is the aspect of each planet to every other planet, where for example two planets 120&#176; apart (in \'trine\') are in a harmonious relationship, but two planets 90&#176; apart (\'square\') are in a conflicted relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Together these relationships and their interpretations supposedly form  "...the language of the heavens speaking to learned men."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kremer_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kremer-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarot_divination" title="Tarot divination">tarot divination</a>, astrology is one of the core studies of <a href="/wiki/Western_esotericism" title="Western esotericism">Western esotericism</a>, and as such has influenced systems of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magic_(paranormal)" title="Magic (paranormal)">magical</a> belief not only among Western esotericists and <a href="/wiki/Hermeticism" title="Hermeticism">Hermeticists</a>, but also belief systems such as <a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wicca</a> that have borrowed from or been influenced by the Western esoteric tradition. <a href="/wiki/Tanya_Luhrmann" title="Tanya Luhrmann">Tanya Luhrmann</a> has said that "all magicians know something about astrology," and refers to a <a href="/wiki/Table_of_correspondences" title="Table of correspondences">table of correspondences</a> in <a href="/wiki/Starhawk" title="Starhawk">Starhawk\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spiral_Dance" title="The Spiral Dance">The Spiral Dance</a></i>, organised by <a href="/wiki/Planets_in_astrology" title="Planets in astrology">planet</a>, as an example of the astrological lore studied by magicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luhrmann_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luhrmann-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindu_2">Hindu</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Hindu astrology</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="475" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg/170px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg/255px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg/340px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Page from an Indian astrological treatise, c. 1750</div></div></div>\n<p>The earliest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veda" title="Veda">Vedic</a> text on astronomy is the <i><a href="/wiki/Vedanga_Jyotisha" title="Vedanga Jyotisha">Vedanga Jyotisha</a></i>; Vedic thought later came to include astrology as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Subbarayappa_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Subbarayappa-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hindu natal astrology originated with Hellenistic astrology by the 3rd century BCE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pingree1978_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pingree1978-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>361</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pingree2001_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pingree2001-95">[95]</a></sup> though incorporating the Hindu lunar mansions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The names of the signs (e.g. Greek \'Krios\' for Aries, Hindi \'Kriya\'), the planets (e.g. Greek \'Helios\' for Sun, astrological Hindi \'Heli\'), and astrological terms (e.g. Greek \'apoklima\' and \'sunaphe\' for declination and planetary conjunction, Hindi \'apoklima\' and \'sunapha\' respectively) in Varaha Mihira\'s texts are considered conclusive evidence of a Greek origin for Hindu astrology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The Indian techniques may also have been augmented with some of the Babylonian techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pingree1963_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pingree1963-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>231</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_and_East-Asian">Chinese and East-Asian</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_zodiac" title="Chinese zodiac">Chinese zodiac</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese astrology</a> has a close relation with <a href="/wiki/Chinese_philosophy" title="Chinese philosophy">Chinese philosophy</a> (theory of the three harmonies: heaven, earth and man) and uses concepts such as <a href="/wiki/Yin_and_yang" title="Yin and yang">yin and yang</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wu_Xing" title="Wu Xing">Five phases</a>, the 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestial_stem" title="Celestial stem">Celestial stems</a>, the 12 <a href="/wiki/Earthly_Branches" title="Earthly Branches">Earthly Branches</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_units_of_measurement" title="Chinese units of measurement">shichen</a> (&#26178;&#36784; a form of timekeeping used for religious purposes). The early use of Chinese astrology was mainly confined to <a href="/wiki/History_of_astrology" title="History of astrology">political astrology</a>, the observation of unusual phenomena, identification of <a href="/wiki/Omen" title="Omen">portents</a> and the selection of auspicious days for events and decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kistemaker_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kistemaker-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>22,85,176</span></sup>\n</p><p>The constellations of the Zodiac of western Asia and Europe were not used; instead the sky is divided into <a href="/wiki/Chinese_constellations" title="Chinese constellations">Three Enclosures</a> (&#19977;&#22435; s&#257;n yu&#225;n), and <a href="/wiki/Twenty-Eight_Mansions" title="Twenty-Eight Mansions">Twenty-Eight Mansions</a> (&#20108;&#21313;&#20843;&#23487; &#232;rsh&#237;b&#257; xi&#249;) in twelve Ci (<a class="extiw" href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%88%86%E9%87%8E" title="zh:&#20998;&#37326;">&#21313;&#20108;&#27425;</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The Chinese zodiac of twelve <a href="/wiki/Astrological_sign#Chinese_zodiac_signs" title="Astrological sign">animal signs</a> is said to represent twelve different types of <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a>. It is based on cycles of years, lunar months, and two-hour periods of the day (the shichen). The zodiac traditionally begins with the sign of the <a href="/wiki/Rat_(zodiac)" title="Rat (zodiac)">Rat</a>, and the cycle proceeds through 11 other animals signs: the <a href="/wiki/Ox_(zodiac)" title="Ox (zodiac)">Ox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiger_(zodiac)" title="Tiger (zodiac)">Tiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabbit_(zodiac)" title="Rabbit (zodiac)">Rabbit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dragon_(zodiac)" title="Dragon (zodiac)">Dragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snake_(zodiac)" title="Snake (zodiac)">Snake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_(zodiac)" title="Horse (zodiac)">Horse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat_(zodiac)" title="Goat (zodiac)">Goat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monkey_(zodiac)" title="Monkey (zodiac)">Monkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rooster_(zodiac)" title="Rooster (zodiac)">Rooster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dog_(zodiac)" title="Dog (zodiac)">Dog</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pig_(zodiac)" title="Pig (zodiac)">Pig</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Complex systems of predicting fate and destiny based on one\'s birthday, birth season, and birth hours, such as <i>ziping</i> and <a href="/wiki/Zi_wei_dou_shu" title="Zi wei dou shu">Zi Wei Dou Shu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">&#32043;&#24494;&#26007;&#25968;</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">&#32043;&#24494;&#26007;&#25976;</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">z&#464;w&#275;id&#466;ush&#249;</span></i>) are still used regularly in modern-day Chinese astrology. They do not rely on direct observations of the stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_zodiac" title="Korean zodiac">Korean zodiac</a> is identical to the Chinese one. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_zodiac" title="Vietnamese zodiac">Vietnamese zodiac</a> is almost identical to Chinese zodiac except the second animal is the <i><a href="/wiki/Water_buffalo_(zodiac)" title="Water buffalo (zodiac)">Water Buffalo</a></i> instead of the <i><a href="/wiki/Ox_(zodiac)" title="Ox (zodiac)">Ox</a></i>, and the fourth animal is the <i><a href="/wiki/Cat_(zodiac)" title="Cat (zodiac)">Cat</a></i> instead of the <i><a href="/wiki/Rabbit_(zodiac)" title="Rabbit (zodiac)">Rabbit</a></i>. The Japanese have since 1873 celebrated the beginning of the new year on 1 January as per the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>. The Thai zodiac begins, not at <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a>, but either on the first day of fifth month in the <a href="/wiki/Thai_lunar_calendar" title="Thai lunar calendar">Thai lunar calendar</a>, or during the <a href="/wiki/Songkran_(Thailand)" title="Songkran (Thailand)">Songkran</a> festival (now celebrated every 13&#8211;15 April), depending on the purpose of the use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theological_viewpoints">Theological viewpoints</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_astrology" title="Christian views on astrology">Christian views on astrology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_views_on_astrology" title="Jewish views on astrology">Jewish views on astrology</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_views_on_astrology" title="Muslim views on astrology">Muslim views on astrology</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span></h3>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Augustine" title="St. Augustine">St. Augustine</a> (354&#8211;430) believed that the determinism of astrology conflicted with the Christian doctrines of man\'s free will and responsibility, and God not being the cause of evil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> but he also grounded his opposition philosophically, citing the failure of astrology to explain twins who behave differently although conceived at the same moment and born at approximately the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hess_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hess-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">Medieval</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avicenna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="301" decoding="async" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Avicenna.jpg/170px-Avicenna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Avicenna.jpg/255px-Avicenna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Avicenna.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avicenna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A drawing of Avicenna</div></div></div><p>\nSome of the practices of astrology were contested on theological grounds by medieval Muslim astronomers such as <a href="/wiki/Al-Farabi" title="Al-Farabi">Al-Farabi</a> (Alpharabius), <a href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Haytham" title="Ibn al-Haytham">Ibn al-Haytham</a> (Alhazen) and <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a>. They said that the methods of astrologers conflicted with orthodox religious views of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulema" title="Ulema">Islamic scholars</a>, by suggesting that the Will of God can be known and predicted in advance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> For example, Avicenna\'s \'Refutation against astrology\', <i>Ris&#257;la f&#299; ib&#7789;&#257;l a&#7717;k&#257;m al-noj&#363;m</i>, argues against the practice of astrology while supporting the principle that planets may act as agents of divine causation. Avicenna considered that the movement of the planets influenced life on earth in a deterministic way, but argued against the possibility of determining the exact influence of the stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Essentially, Avicenna did not deny the core dogma of astrology, but denied our ability to understand it to the extent that precise and fatalistic predictions could be made from it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Qayyim_Al-Jawziyya" title="Ibn Qayyim Al-Jawziyya">Ibn Qayyim Al-Jawziyya</a> (1292&#8211;1350), in his <i>Miftah Dar al-SaCadah</i>, also used <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physical</a> arguments in astronomy to question the practice of judicial astrology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livingston_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Livingston-108">[108]</a></sup> He recognised that the <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">stars</a> are much larger than the <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planets</a>, and argued: </p><blockquote><p>And if you astrologers answer that it is precisely because of this distance and smallness that their influences are negligible, then why is it that you claim a great influence for the smallest heavenly body, Mercury? Why is it that you have given an influence to al-Ra\'s and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Dhanab" title="Al-Dhanab">al-Dhanab</a>, which are two imaginary points [ascending and descending nodes]?<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livingston_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Livingston-108">[108]</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">Maimonides</a>, the preeminent Jewish philosopher, astronomer, and legal codifier, wrote that astrology is forbidden by Jewish law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">Modern</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catechism_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Catechism of the Catholic Church">Catechism of the Catholic Church</a> maintains that divination, including predictive astrology, is incompatible with modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> beliefs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> such as free will:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hess_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hess-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>All forms of divination are to be rejected: recourse to Satan or demons, conjuring up the dead or other practices falsely supposed to "unveil" the future. Consulting horoscopes, astrology, palm reading, interpretation of omens and lots, the phenomena of clairvoyance, and recourse to mediums all conceal a desire for power over time, history, and, in the last analysis, other human beings, as well as a wish to conciliate hidden powers. They contradict the honor, respect, and loving fear that we owe to God alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>Catechism of the Catholic Church</cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_analysis_and_criticism">Scientific analysis and criticism</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Astrology_and_science" title="Astrology and science">Astrology and science</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karl_Popper.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="769" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Karl_Popper.jpg/170px-Karl_Popper.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Karl_Popper.jpg/255px-Karl_Popper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Karl_Popper.jpg/340px-Karl_Popper.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karl_Popper.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Popper proposed falsifiability as something that distinguishes science from non-science, using astrology as the example of an idea that has not dealt with falsification during experiment</div></div></div>\n<p>The scientific community rejects astrology as having no explanatory power for describing the universe, and considers it a <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SandPSandAstroSoc_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-SandPSandAstroSoc-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astrosociety.org_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-astrosociety.org-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hartmann_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hartmann-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>1350</span></sup> Scientific testing of astrology has been conducted, and no evidence has been found to support any of the premises or purported effects outlined in astrological traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zarka_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zarka-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>424;</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> There is no proposed <a href="/wiki/Scientific_modelling" title="Scientific modelling">mechanism of action</a> by which the positions and motions of stars and planets could affect people and events on Earth that does not contradict well understood, basic aspects of biology and physics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vishveshwara_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vishveshwara-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>249;</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AsquithNSF_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-AsquithNSF-8">[8]</a></sup>  Those who continue to have faith in astrology have been characterised as doing so "...in spite of the fact that there is no verified scientific basis for their beliefs, and indeed that there is strong evidence to the contrary."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humanist_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Humanist-114">[114]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Confirmation_bias" title="Confirmation bias">Confirmation bias</a> is a form of <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_bias" title="Cognitive bias">cognitive bias</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychological</a> factor that contributes to belief in astrology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allum_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allum-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>344;</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymond_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raymond-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>180&#8211;181;</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eysenck1982_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eysenck1982-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>42&#8211;48</span></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[a]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez-119">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>553</span></sup> Astrology believers tend to selectively remember predictions that turn out to be true, and do not remember those that turn out false.
